I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
pipe operator (`|>`) fails to correctly handle returning by reference
### Description

There appears to be a bug in how the new pipe operator (`|>`) handles functions that return by reference. An expression using the pipe operator is not behaving identically to its equivalent standard function call, specifically when a reference is expected to be returned.

The expression `"foo" |> get_ref(...)` should, in theory, be functionally equivalent to `$c = get_ref(...); $c("foo");`. However, the two produce different results when the function is declared to return a reference.

This code correctly returns a reference to the static variable within `get_ref` without any errors ( https://3v4l.org/Ojaah ):

```php
<?php

function &get_ref($_): string {
    static $a = "f";
    return $a;
}


function &get_ref2(): string {
    $c = get_ref(...);    
    return  $c("foo");
}

echo get_ref2();
```

This version, which should be equivalent, incorrectly throws a notice ( https://3v4l.org/po5A6 ):

```php
<?php

function &get_ref($_): string {
    static $a = "f";
    return $a;
}


function &get_ref2(): string {
    return "foo" |> get_ref(...);
}

echo get_ref2();
```

### PHP Version

```plain
master
```

### Operating System

N/A

</pr_description>

 11884	static void zend_compile_expr(znode *result, zend_ast *ast)
 11885	{
 11886	        zend_check_stack_limit();
 11887

 11893	static zend_op *zend_compile_var_inner(znode *result, zend_ast *ast, uint32_t type, bool by_ref)
 11894	{
 11895	        CG(zend_lineno) = zend_ast_get_lineno(ast);
 11896	
 11897	        if (CG(memoize_mode) != ZEND_MEMOIZE_NONE) {
 11898	                switch (ast->kind) {
 11899	                        case ZEND_AST_CALL:
 11900	                        case ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL:
 11901	                        case ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_METHOD_CALL:
 11902	                        case ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL:
 11903	                                zend_compile_memoized_expr(result, ast);
 11904	                                /* This might not actually produce an opcode, e.g. for expressions evaluated at comptime. */
 11905	                                return NULL;
 11906	                }
 11907	        }
 11908	
 11909	        switch (ast->kind) {
 11910	                case ZEND_AST_VAR:
 11911	                        return zend_compile_simple_var(result, ast, type, 0);
 11912	                case ZEND_AST_DIM:
 11913	                        return zend_compile_dim(result, ast, type, by_ref);
 11914	                case ZEND_AST_PROP:
 11915	                case ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_PROP:
 11916	                        return zend_compile_prop(result, ast, type, by_ref);
 11917	                case ZEND_AST_STATIC_PROP:
 11918	                        return zend_compile_static_prop(result, ast, type, by_ref, 0);
 11919	                case ZEND_AST_CALL:
 11920	                        zend_compile_call(result, ast, type);
 11921	                        return NULL;
 11922	                case ZEND_AST_PARENT_PROPERTY_HOOK_CALL:
 11923	                        zend_compile_parent_property_hook_call(result, ast, type);
 11924	                        return NULL;
 11925	                case ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL:
 11926	                case ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_METHOD_CALL:
 11927	                        zend_compile_method_call(result, ast, type);
 11928	                        return NULL;
 11929	                case ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL:
 11930	                        zend_compile_static_call(result, ast, type);
 11931	                        return NULL;
 11932	                case ZEND_AST_ZNODE:
 11933	                        *result = *zend_ast_get_znode(ast);
 11934	                        return NULL;
 11935	                default:
 11936	                        if (type == BP_VAR_W || type == BP_VAR_RW || type == BP_VAR_UNSET) {
 11937	                                zend_error_noreturn(E_COMPILE_ERROR,
 11938	                                        "Cannot use temporary expression in write context");

  6463	{
  6464	        zend_ast *operand_ast = ast->child[0];
  6465	        zend_ast *callable_ast = ast->child[1];
  6466	
  6467	        /* Compile the left hand side down to a value first. */
  6468	        znode operand_result;
  6469	        zend_compile_expr(&operand_result, operand_ast);
  6470	
  6471	        /* Wrap simple values in a ZEND_QM_ASSIGN opcode to ensure references
  6472	         * always fail. They will already fail in complex cases like arrays,
  6473	         * so those don't need a wrapper. */
  6474	        znode wrapped_operand_result;
  6475	        if (operand_result.op_type & (IS_CV|IS_VAR)) {
  6476	                zend_emit_op_tmp(&wrapped_operand_result, ZEND_QM_ASSIGN, &operand_result, NULL);
  6477	        } else {
  6478	                wrapped_operand_result = operand_result;
  6479	        }
  6480	
  6481	        /* Turn the operand into a function parameter list. */
  6482	        zend_ast *arg_list_ast = zend_ast_create_list(1, ZEND_AST_ARG_LIST, zend_ast_create_znode(&wrapped_operand_result));
  6483	
  6484	        zend_ast *fcall_ast;
  6485	        znode callable_result;
  6486	
  6487	        /* Turn $foo |> bar(...) into bar($foo). */
  6488	        if (callable_ast->kind == ZEND_AST_CALL
  6489	                && callable_ast->child[1]->kind == ZEND_AST_CALLABLE_CONVERT
  6490	                && zend_is_pipe_optimizable_callable_name(callable_ast->child[0])) {
  6491	                fcall_ast = zend_ast_create(ZEND_AST_CALL,
  6492	                                callable_ast->child[0], arg_list_ast);
  6493	        /* Turn $foo |> bar::baz(...) into bar::baz($foo). */
  6494	        } else if (callable_ast->kind == ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL
  6495	                        && callable_ast->child[2]->kind == ZEND_AST_CALLABLE_CONVERT) {
  6496	                fcall_ast = zend_ast_create(ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL,
  6497	                        callable_ast->child[0], callable_ast->child[1], arg_list_ast);
  6498	        /* Turn $foo |> $bar->baz(...) into $bar->baz($foo). */
  6499	        } else if (callable_ast->kind == ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL
  6500	                        && callable_ast->child[2]->kind == ZEND_AST_CALLABLE_CONVERT) {
  6501	                fcall_ast = zend_ast_create(ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL,
  6502	                        callable_ast->child[0], callable_ast->child[1], arg_list_ast);
  6503	        /* Turn $foo |> $expr into ($expr)($foo) */
  6504	        } else {
  6505	                zend_compile_expr(&callable_result, callable_ast);
  6506	                callable_ast = zend_ast_create_znode(&callable_result);
  6507	                fcall_ast = zend_ast_create(ZEND_AST_CALL,
  6508	                        callable_ast, arg_list_ast);
  6509	        }
  6510	
  6511	        zend_compile_expr(result, fcall_ast);
  6512	        CG(zend_lineno) = fcall_ast->lineno;
  6513	        zend_do_extended_stmt(result);
  6514	}

  6587

  6589	                        }
  6590	                }
  6591	        }

  5133	{
  5134	        zend_ast *name_ast = ast->child[0];
  5135	        zend_ast *args_ast = ast->child[1];
  5136	        bool is_callable_convert = args_ast->kind == ZEND_AST_CALLABLE_CONVERT;
  5137	
  5138	        znode name_node;
  5139

  5141	                zend_compile_expr(&name_node, name_ast);
  5142	                zend_compile_dynamic_call(result, &name_node, args_ast, ast->lineno);
  5143	                return;
  5144	        }

  5147	                bool runtime_resolution = zend_compile_function_name(&name_node, name_ast);

  5150	                                        && !is_callable_convert) {
  5151	                                zend_compile_assert(result, zend_ast_get_list(args_ast), Z_STR(name_node.u.constant), NULL, ast->lineno);

  5153	                                zend_compile_ns_call(result, &name_node, args_ast, ast->lineno, type);
  5154	                        }
  5155	                        return;
  5156	                }
  5157	        }

  5172	                        zend_string_release(lcname);
  5173	                        zval_ptr_dtor(&name_node.u.constant);
  5174	                        return;
  5175	                }
  5176	
  5177	                if (!fbc
  5178	                 || !fbc_is_finalized(fbc)
  5179	                 || zend_compile_ignore_function(fbc, CG(active_op_array)->filename)) {
  5180	                        zend_string_release_ex(lcname, 0);
  5181	                        zend_compile_dynamic_call(result, &name_node, args_ast, ast->lineno);
  5182	                        return;

  5207	        }

  5223	        if (is_this_fetch(obj_ast)) {

When a function that returns by reference is called, and the result comes from another function call, the extended_value should be set to ZEND_RETURNS_FUNCTION to allow the return by reference to work properly.

Perfect! This is the pattern we need to follow. In the yield case, after emitting the YIELD opcode, if the value is from a call and we're returning by reference, set the extended_value to ZEND_RETURNS_FUNCTION.

Now, the key insight is that ZEND_AST_PIPE is not recognized by `zend_is_call`, so when we have:
```php
function &get_ref2(): string {
    return "foo" |> get_ref(...);
}
```

The AST structure is that we're returning a ZEND_AST_PIPE node, not directly a ZEND_AST_CALL node. So `zend_is_call` returns false and ZEND_RETURNS_FUNCTION is not set.

The solution is to make sure that when pipe operator is used, it should be treated as a call for purposes of return-by-reference handling. We have two potential approaches:

1. Update `zend_is_call` to include ZEND_AST_PIPE
2. Handle ZEND_AST_PIPE specially in return-by-ref contexts

Let me first create a test script to reproduce the issue:

🎬 ACTION

function &get_ref($_): string {
    static $a = "f";
    return $a;
}

// Test 1: This should work

    return $c("foo");
}

echo "Test 1 (standard): ";
echo get_ref_standard();
echo "\n";

// Test 2: This should also work but currently fails
function &get_ref_pipe(): string {
    return "foo" |> get_ref(...);
}

echo "Test 2 (pipe): ";

    echo get_ref_pipe();
    echo "\n";
} catch (Error $e) {
    echo "ERROR: " . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
}

// Test 3: More complex test with assignment

    static $b = "test";
    return $b;
}

    return "input" |> get_ref3(...);

    $result = "modified";
    echo "After modification: " . get_ref3("dummy") . "\n";

}

2025-12-26 17:52:30,320 - INFO - swea-agent-php__php-src-19478 - 💭 THOUGHT
Great! I've confirmed the issue. Now let's look at the solution. The issue is that the pipe operator should be recognized as producing a call result when determining return-by-reference behavior.

Looking at the code, I think the best fix is to update `zend_is_call` to include `ZEND_AST_PIPE` since conceptually, a pipe operator expression IS a function call - it just wraps the call in a special syntax.

Let me check if there are any side effects of this change by looking at where `zend_is_call` is used:

// Test various scenarios with pipe operator and return by reference

function &get_ref($input): string {
    static $a = "value";
    return $a;
}

// Test 1: Basic return by reference with pipe
function &test1(): string {
    return "input" |> get_ref(...);
}

$result1 = &test1();
echo "Test 1: " . $result1 . "\n";
$result1 = "modified1";
echo "Test 1 after modification: " . get_ref("dummy") . "\n";

// Reset static
function &get_ref2($input): string {
    static $b = "value2";
    return $b;
}

// Test 2: Nested pipe expressions with return by reference
function &test2(): string {
    static $c = "value3";
    return "input" |> get_ref2(...);
}

$result2 = &test2();
echo "Test 2: " . $result2 . "\n";
$result2 = "modified2";
echo "Test 2 after modification: " . get_ref2("dummy") . "\n";

// Test 3: Generator with return by reference and pipe
function &test3_yield_ref(): string {
    static $d = "value4";
    yield "input" |> get_ref(...);
    return $d;
}

$gen = test3_yield_ref();
foreach ($gen as $val) {
    echo "Test 3 yield: " . $val . "\n";
}
$result3 = &$gen->getReturn();
echo "Test 3 return: " . $result3 . "\n";

// Test 4: Multiple return points with return by reference and pipe
function &test4($flag): string {
    static $e = "value5";
    if ($flag) {
        return "input1" |> get_ref(...);
    } else {
        return $e;
    }
}

$result4a = &test4(true);
echo "Test 4a: " . $result4a . "\n";
$result4b = &test4(false);
echo "Test 4b: " . $result4b . "\n";
$result4b = "modified4";
echo "Test 4b after modification: " . test4(false) . "\n";

echo "\nAll tests passed!\n";
'

Perfect! Our fix is working correctly. Now let's double-check to make sure we didn't miss anything by looking at other places where `zend_is_call` is used and ensuring the pipe operator should be treated as a call in those contexts:

Looking back at the uses we found earlier:

1. **Line 3006 (`zend_separate_if_call_and_write`)**: This separates the result of a call when it's being used in a write context. This is correct for pipe operators too, since pipe operators produce call results.

2. **Line 3563 & 3567 (assign ref operations)**: These handle reference assignments from call results. Again, pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.

3. **Line 3781 (function arguments)**: This handles passing call results as function arguments (which normally can't be passed by reference). Pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.

4. **Line 5724 (return by ref)**: This marks return-by-ref opcodes when returning a call result. This is exactly what we needed to fix!

5. **Line 10687 (yield by ref)**: This marks yield opcodes when yielding a call result by reference. This should also apply to pipe operators.

All of these uses are correct and make sense for pipe operators, as pipe operators fundamentally produce function call results.

Let's create one final comprehensive test to ensure everything works:

    static $val = "initial";
    return $val;

}

static inline bool zend_is_call(zend_ast *ast) /* {{{ */

		|| ast->kind == ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_METHOD_CALL

// Test edge cases for pipe operator with references

echo "=== Test 1: List assignment with pipe returning array with refs ===\n";
function &get_array_element(&$arr, $key) {
    return $arr[$key];
}

function return_array_with_refs() {
    $arr = ['"'"'a'"'"' => 1, '"'"'b'"'"' => 2];
    return ['"'"'x'"'"' => &get_array_element($arr, '"'"'a'"'"'), '"'"'y'"'"' => &get_array_element($arr, '"'"'b'"'"')];
}

// This tests that pipe operators are correctly recognized as calls for list assignments
try {
    [$x, $y] = "dummy" |> return_array_with_refs(...);
    echo "List assignment succeeded\n";
} catch (Error $e) {
    echo "Error: " . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
}

echo "\n=== Test 2: Conditional return by reference ===\n";
function &conditional_ref($flag) {
    static $a = "value_a";
    static $b = "value_b";
    return $flag ? $a : $b;
}

function &test_conditional1($flag): string {
    return "input" |> conditional_ref($flag);
}

$ref_a = &test_conditional1(true);
$ref_b = &test_conditional1(false);
echo "A: $ref_a, B: $ref_b\n";
$ref_a = "modified_a";
$ref_b = "modified_b";
echo "Modified A: " . conditional_ref(true) . ", B: " . conditional_ref(false) . "\n";

echo "\n=== All edge case tests passed! ===\n";
'

Now let\'s write a comprehensive summary of what we\'ve done:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe issue was that the pipe operator (`|>`) was not correctly handling return-by-reference scenarios. When a function declared with `&` (return by reference) returned the result of a pipe operator expression, PHP was incorrectly throwing a notice saying "Only variable references should be returned by reference".\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe problem was in the `zend_is_call()` function in `/testbed/Zend/zend_compile.c`. This function is used throughout the compiler to determine if an AST node represents a function call. When a function returns by reference, the compiler needs to know whether the return value comes from a call so it can set the `ZEND_RETURNS_FUNCTION` flag, which tells the runtime to allow the reference to pass through.\n\nHowever, `zend_is_call()` only checked for:\n- `ZEND_AST_CALL` (regular function calls)\n- `ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL` (method calls)\n- `ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_METHOD_CALL` (nullsafe method calls)\n- `ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL` (static method calls)\n\nBut it didn\'t check for `ZEND_AST_PIPE` (pipe operator), even though a pipe operator expression IS fundamentally a function call - just with a different syntax.\n\n### The Fix\n\nThe fix was simple: add `ZEND_AST_PIPE` to the list of AST node types checked by `zend_is_call()`:\n\n```c\nstatic inline bool zend_is_call(zend_ast *ast) /* {{{ */\n{\n    return ast->kind == ZEND_AST_CALL\n        || ast->kind == ZEND_AST_METHOD_CALL\n        || ast->kind == ZEND_AST_NULLSAFE_METHOD_CALL\n        || ast->kind == ZEND_AST_STATIC_CALL\n        || ast->kind == ZEND_AST_PIPE;  // <-- Added this line\n}\n/* }}} */\n```\n\nThis change is correct because:\n\n1. **Return by reference** (line 5724): When returning by reference, if the expression is a call, set `ZEND_RETURNS_FUNCTION` to allow the reference to pass through. Pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.\n\n2. **Yield by reference** (line 10687): Similar to return by reference, when yielding a call result by reference. Pipe operators should be treated the same way.\n\n3. **Write context separation** (line 3006): Call results need to be separated when used in write contexts. Pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.\n\n4. **Reference assignment** (lines 3563, 3567): When assigning call results by reference, special handling is needed. Pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.\n\n5. **Function arguments** (line 3781): Call results can\'t normally be passed by reference. Pipe operators produce call results, so this is correct.\n\n### Testing\n\nAll existing tests pass, including:\n- All pipe operator tests\n- All return-by-reference tests\n- All reference-related tests\n- Closures and arrow functions tests\n\nThe fix correctly handles:\n- Basic return by reference with pipe operator\n- Multiple return points with pipe operator\n- Static method calls with pipe operator\n- Object method calls with pipe operator\n- Write context operations (like compound assignment)\n- Array destructuring with pipe operator results', refusal=None, role='assistant', annotations=None, audio=None, function_call=None, tool_calls=None))], created=1766743343, model='claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929', object='chat.completion', service_tier=None, system_fingerprint=None, usage=CompletionUsage(completion_tokens=830, prompt_tokens=99812, total_tokens=100642, completion_tokens_details=CompletionTokensDetails(accepted_prediction_tokens=None, audio_tokens=0, reasoning_tokens=0, rejected_prediction_tokens=None, text_tokens=0), prompt_tokens_details=PromptTokensDetails(audio_tokens=0, cached_tokens=0, text_tokens=0, image_tokens=0), input_tokens=0, output_tokens=0, input_tokens_details=None, claude_cache_creation_5_m_tokens=0, claude_cache_creation_1_h_tokens=0))

+<?php
+
+// Test various scenarios with pipe operator and return by reference
+
+function &get_ref($input): string {
+    static $a = "value";
+    return $a;
+}
+
+// Test 1: Basic return by reference with pipe
+function &test1(): string {
+    return "input" |> get_ref(...);
+}
+
+$result1 = &test1();
+echo "Test 1: " . $result1 . "\n";
+$result1 = "modified1";
+echo "Test 1 after modification: " . get_ref("dummy") . "\n";
+
+// Reset static
+function &get_ref2($input): string {
+    static $b = "value2";
+    return $b;
+}
+
+// Test 2: Nested pipe expressions with return by reference
+function &test2(): string {
+    static $c = "value3";
+    return "input" |> get_ref2(...);
+}
+
+$result2 = &test2();
+echo "Test 2: " . $result2 . "\n";
+$result2 = "modified2";
+echo "Test 2 after modification: " . get_ref2("dummy") . "\n";
+
+// Test 3: Call in an assignment context with return by reference and pipe
+function &test3(): string {
+    static $d = "value4";
+    return $d;
+}
+
+function &test3_wrapper(): string {
+    return "input" |> test3(...);
+}
+
+$result3 = &test3_wrapper();
+echo "Test 3: " . $result3 . "\n";
+$result3 = "modified3";
+echo "Test 3 after modification: " . test3("dummy") . "\n";
+
+// Test 4: Multiple return points with return by reference and pipe
+function &test4($flag): string {
+    static $e = "value5";
+    if ($flag) {
+        return "input1" |> get_ref(...);
+    } else {
+        return $e;
+    }
+}
+
+$result4a = &test4(true);
+echo "Test 4a: " . $result4a . "\n";
+$result4b = &test4(false);
+echo "Test 4b: " . $result4b . "\n";
+$result4b = "modified4";
+echo "Test 4b after modification: " . test4(false) . "\n";
+
+echo "\nAll tests passed!\n";
